<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_legacy">Global legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afonso_de_Albuquerque&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Global legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The fabled <a href="/wiki/Maluku_Islands" title="Maluku Islands">Spice Islands</a> were on the imagination of Europe since ancient times. In the 2nd century AD, Malaya was known by the Greek philosopher <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy" title="Ptolemy">Ptolemy</a>, who labeled it 'Aurea Chersonesus"; and who said that it was believed the fabled area held gold in abundance. Even Indian traders referred to the East Pacific region as "Land of Gold" and made regular visits to Malaya in search of the precious metal, tin and sweet scented jungle woods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> But neither Ptolemy, nor Rome, nor Alexander was able to see the fabled regions of the East Pacific. Afonso de Albuquerque became the first European to reach the Spice Islands. Upon discovering <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, he proceeded in 1511 to conquer Malacca, then commissioned an expedition under the command of <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Abreu" title="António de Abreu">António de Abreu</a> and Vice-Commander <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Serr%C3%A3o" title="Francisco Serrão">Francisco Serrão</a> (the latter being a cousin of Magellan) to further explore the extremities of the region in east Indonesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> As a result of these voyages of exploration, the Portuguese became the first Europeans to discover and to reach the fabled Spice Islands of Malaysia, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indies" title="Indies">Indies</a> in addition to discovering their sea routes. Afonso found what had evaded Columbus' grasp — the wealth of the Orient. His discoveries did not go unnoticed, and it took little time for <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">Magellan</a> to arrive in the same region a few years later and discover the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> for Spain, giving birth to the Papal <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Zaragoza" title="Treaty of Zaragoza">Treaty of Zaragoza</a>.</p>
<p>Afonso's operations sent a voyage pushing further south which made the European discovery of Timor in the far south of Oceania, and the discovery of <a href="/wiki/History_of_Papua_New_Guinea" title="History of Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> in 1512. This was followed up by another Portuguese, <a href="/wiki/Jorge_de_Menezes" title="Jorge de Menezes">Jorge de Menezes</a> in 1526, who named Papua New Guinea, the "Island of the Papua".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_discoveries_and_explorationsV2en.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1357" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Portuguese_discoveries_and_explorationsV2en.png/300px-Portuguese_discoveries_and_explorationsV2en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Portuguese_discoveries_and_explorationsV2en.png/450px-Portuguese_discoveries_and_explorationsV2en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Portuguese_discoveries_and_explorationsV2en.png/600px-Portuguese_discoveries_and_explorationsV2en.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_discoveries_and_explorationsV2en.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese discoveries</a> and explorations: first arrival places and dates; main Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">spice trade</a> routes in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> (blue)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Through Alfonso's diplomatic activities, Portugal opened the sea between Europe and China. As early as 1513, Jorge de Albuquerque, a Portuguese commanding officer in Malacca, sent his subordinate <a href="/wiki/Jorge_%C3%81lvares" title="Jorge Álvares">Jorge Álvares</a> to sail to China on a ship loaded with pepper from Sumatra. After sailing across the sea, Jorge Álvares and his crew dropped anchor in Tamao, an island located at the mouth of the Pearl River. This was the first Portuguese to set foot in the territory known as China, the mythical "Middle Kingdom" where they erected a stone <a href="/wiki/Padr%C3%A3o" title="Padrão">Padrão</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Álvares is the first European to reach Chinese land by sea,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> and, the first European to enter Hong Kong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> In 1514 Afonso de Albuquerque, the Viceroy of the Estado da India dispatched <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Perestrello" title="Rafael Perestrello">Rafael Perestrello</a> to sail to China in order to pioneer European trade relations with the Chinese nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Rafael Perestrelo was quoted as saying, "being a very good and honest people, the Chinese hope to make friends with the Portuguese."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-china_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-china-93">[93]</a></sup> In spite of initial harmony and excitement between the two empires, difficulties soon arose.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smithsonianmag.com_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-smithsonianmag.com-94">[94]</a></sup> Portugal's efforts in establishing lasting ties with China did pay off in the long run; the Portuguese colonized Macau, and established the first European permanent settlement on Chinese soil, which served as a permanent colonial base in southern China, and the two empires maintained an exchange in culture and trade for nearly 500 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> The longest empire in history (1515–1999), begun by Alfonso de Albuquerque five centuries earlier, ended when Portugal ceded the government of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Macau" title="Portuguese Macau">Macau</a> to China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-golisbon.com_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-golisbon.com-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>Afonso de Albuquerque pioneered trade relations with Thailand, and was as such the first recorded European to contact Thailand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles_and_honours">Titles and honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afonso_de_Albuquerque&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Titles and honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_governors_of_Portuguese_India" title="List of governors of Portuguese India">Governor and Captain-General of the Seas of India</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_governors_of_Portuguese_India" title="List of governors of Portuguese India">2nd Governor of India</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Goa" title="Duke of Goa">1st Duke of Goa</a></li>
<li>A knight of the Portuguese <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Order_of_Saint_James_of_the_Sword" title="Order of Saint James of the Sword">Order of Saint James of the Sword</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fidalgo" title="Fidalgo">Fidalgo</a> of the Royal Household</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Son">Son</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afonso_de_Albuquerque&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Son">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Afonso de Albuquerque had a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legitimacy_(law)" title="Legitimacy (law)">bastard son</a> with an unrecorded woman. He legitimized the boy in February 1506. Before his death, he asked King Manuel I to leave to the son all his wealth and that the King oversee the son's education. When Alfonso died, Manuel I renamed the child "Afonso" in his father's memory. Brás Afonso de Albuquerque, or Braz in the old spelling, was born in 1500 and died in 1580.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry">Ancestry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afonso_de_Albuquerque&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Ancestry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Carter, Laraine Newhouse (1 January 1991). <i>Persian Gulf States: Chapter 1B. <li id="cite_note-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-34">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Afonso, like many others since then, took office as governor: when appointing the Viceroy Francisco de Almeida, the King promised not to appoint another in his lifetime, a vote of confidence in contradiction with the short term of three years he gave him, that may be due to the great fears about the sharing of power that this position represented.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-35">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the first months of 1508, the son of D. Francisco de Almeida, <a href="/wiki/Louren%C3%A7o_de_Almeida" title="Lourenço de Almeida">Lourenço de Almeida</a>, died in dramatic circumstances at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chaul" title="Battle of Chaul">Battle of Chaul</a> and there are reports that the viceroy, an enlightened and incorruptible ruler, turned vindictive and cruel.</span></li>

Na Regia Officina Typografica.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAfonso+de+Albuquerque&amp;rft.au=Afonso+de+Albuquerque&amp;rft.btitle=Commentarios+do+grande+Afonso+Dalboquerque%3A+capit%C3%A3o+geral+que+foi+das+Indias+Orientaes+em+tempo+do+muito+poderoso+rey+D.+Manuel%2C+o+primeiro+deste+nome&amp;rft.date=1774&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2F%3Fid%3D4UILAAAAYAAJ&amp;rft.pub=Na+Regia+Officina+Typografica&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></li>
